    A sufficient sum of money shall be allocated and set aside from available funds for the purpose of carrying out the provisions of TMRS Act, V.T.C.A., Government Code ch. 851 et seq. Such money, so allocated and set aside, shall be known as the City of Taylor Lake Village Social Security Fund, which fund shall be set aside and maintained in the regular city depository. 
(Ord. No. 89-289, § 4, 2-15-89) 
Secs. 2-130-2-145. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - RECORDS MANAGEMENT 

Sec. 2-146. - Title, policy and purpose of article. 
    This article shall be known and cited as the "Records and Information Management Ordinance for the City of Taylor Lake Village, Texas." It is hereby declared to be the policy of the city to develop a records and information management program that provides for efficient, economical and effective control over the creation, distribution, organization, maintenance, use and disposition of all city records through a comprehensive system of integrated procedures for the management of records from their creation to their ultimate disposition. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 1, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-147. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    City record means a local government record, as set forth in V.T.C.A., Government Code § 441.151(8). 
    Director and librarian means the executive and administrative officer of the state library and archives commission. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 2, 11-7-90) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 2-148. - City records declared public property. 
    All city records are hereby declared to be property of the city. No city officer or employee shall have, by virtue of his office or employment, any personal or property right to any such records even though he may have developed or compiled them. No person shall destroy, remove or use any city record except as authorized by law, this article or the policies and procedures of the city; provided, however, that no policy or procedure regarding use, removal or destruction of city records shall be adopted which conflicts with this article or applicable state or federal law. Nothing contained in this section shall be construed to authorize the disclosure of city records which are exempt from disclosure under state or federal law. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 3, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-149. - Records and information management responsibility established. 
    There is hereby established a records and information management program. The city secretary shall administer the records and information management program and shall be responsible for city-wide files management. In addition, the city secretary shall have direction and control of the city's records disposition program. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 4, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-150. - Duties of city secretary. 
    The city secretary shall: 
(1)	Assist in establishing and developing policies and procedures for a records management program for the city; 
(2)	Administer the records management program and provide assistance to custodians for the purposes of reducing the costs and improving the efficiency of recordkeeping; 
(3)	In cooperation with the custodians of the records: 
a.	Prepare and file with the director and librarian the records control schedules and amended schedules required by V.T.C.A., Government Code § 203.041, and the list of obsolete records as provided by V.T.C.A., Government Code § 203.444; and 
b.	Prepare or direct the preparation of requests for authorization to destroy records not on an approved control schedule as provided by V.T.C.A., Government Code § 203.045, or requests to destroy the originals of permanent records that have been microfilmed as provided by V.T.C.A., Government Code § 204.008, and of electronic storage authorization requests as provided by V.T.C.A., Government Code § 205.007. 
(4)	In cooperation with custodians, identify and take adequate steps to protect essential city records; 
(5)	In cooperation with custodians, ensure that the maintenance, preservation, microfilming, destruction, or other disposition of city records is carried out in accordance with the policies and procedures of the city's records management program, this article and rules adopted pursuant hereto; 
(6)	Disseminate to the city council and custodians information concerning state laws, administrative rules and the policies of the government relating to local government records; and 
(7)	In cooperation with custodians, establish procedures to ensure that the handling of city records by the records management officer or those under the officer's authority is carried out in compliance with the records management program and with due regard for: 
a.	The duties and responsibilities of custodians that may be imposed by law; and 
b.	The confidentiality of information in records to which access is restricted by law. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 5, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-151. - Responsibilities of city department heads. 
    All city department heads are responsible for the implementation and operation of effective files operations, record transfers and dispositions, and other activities in accordance with the provisions of this article within their areas of responsibility. They shall designate records coordinators within their offices and provide the city secretary the names of such designees and of all file stations and file custodians under their supervision. Persons designated as records coordinators shall report directly to the head of their department on matters relating to the records management program and should have appropriate access to all files in their department. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 6, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-152. - Responsibilities of records coordinators. 
    Each records coordinator shall coordinate the records management program between the city secretary and personnel in the record coordinator's office to ensure that the provisions of this article are followed. This responsibility shall include overseeing the application of records schedules within the office or department. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 7, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-153. - City offices to use record schedules. 
    All city offices and departments shall adopt records retention and disposition schedules and destroy, transfer or otherwise dispose of records only according to such schedules. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 8, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-154. - Development of records retention and disposition schedules. 
(a)	Initial retention periods to be included in records schedules shall be established by the city secretary and department heads. These retention schedules shall be submitted to the city attorney for review who shall notify the city secretary within 15 days of the approval or objection of any retention period. If no objection has been submitted within 15 days, the records schedule shall be adopted and have full force as sufficient authorization for records destruction or other action. If objection is made, the city secretary shall amend the retention period to the satisfaction of the office or department concerned and the city attorney. Revision of retention periods shall be submitted for review to the city attorney in the same manner as the original retention periods. 
(b)	When a records retention and disposition schedule is adopted, it shall thenceforth constitute full authority to destroy, transfer or take other actions, and the city council hereby directs that such actions be taken by the city secretary or under her supervision. The city secretary shall notify the state librarian of the intended destruction, as may be required by law, but no further notice to the city council or other city office shall be required. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 9, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-155. - Destruction of original city records. 
    No original city record shall be destroyed if such destruction is contrary to any state or federal law. Prior to the destruction of any original city record, the city secretary shall obtain the advice and consent of the city attorney. Any original city record, the subject matter of which is in litigations, may not be destroyed until such litigation is final. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 10, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-156. - One-time destruction of obsolete records. 
    Prior to adoption of records schedules for an office, one-time destruction of accumulated obsolete records of that office may be made by or under the supervision of the city secretary. Prior to such destruction the city secretary shall submit lists of records to be destroyed to the department head and the city attorney, who shall give notice within 30 days of any records they believe should not be destroyed, and such records shall be retained for a period agreed upon. The city secretary shall also submit notice as required by law to the state librarian. Obsolete records shall include those no longer created by the office or department and no longer needed for administrative, legal, fiscal or other research purposes. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 11, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-157. - Records center. 
    A records center shall be maintained by the city which shall utilize one or more locations to store inactive records; to ensure the security of such records from deterioration, theft or damage during the period of storage; and to permit fast, efficient retrieval of information from stored records. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 12, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-158. - Preservation of permanent records. 
    The city secretary shall develop procedures to ensure the permanent preservation of historically valuable records of the city. If city-owned facilities are not available, the city secretary shall arrange for the transfer of such records to the state library for perpetual care and preservation in one of its nearby regional historical resource depositories, or shall make other arrangements for their permanent preservation not contrary to law or regulation. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 13, 11-7-90) 
Sec. 2-159. - Noncurrent records not to be maintained in office files. 
    Records no longer required in the conduct of current business by any office of the city shall be promptly transferred to the records center or archives or the state library, or be destroyed at the time such action is designated on an approved records schedule. Such records shall not be maintained in current office files or equipment. 
(Ord. No. 90-309, § 14, 11-7-90) 
Chapter 6 - ANIMALS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Environment, ch. 30. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 6-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Animal control officer means a person in the city hired or contracted for the control and enforcement of this chapter. Police officers of the city are authorized to act as or for the animal control officer. 
    At-large means an animal shall be deemed to be at-large when it is not located on the property of its owner and not under control of a competent person. 
    City pound means any premises designated by the council as the appropriate premises for the purpose of impounding and caring for all animals found to be at-large in violation of this chapter or suspected of being rabid, or known to be rabid. 
    Owner means any person, group of persons or any corporation owning, keeping or harboring an animal. 
    Restraint means controlled by a leash, at heel beside a competent person and obedient to that person's commands, or within a vehicle being driven or parked on the streets, or within the property limits of its owner or keeper. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 1, 1-17-79) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 6-2. - Owner restraint of at-large animals required. 
    All dogs within the city shall be restrained by their owner, or person having control or custody of any dogs, at all times, subject to the exemptions provided herein. It shall be unlawful for any person owning, or having control over, or having custody of any animal to permit or allow such animal to be at-large upon any public roadway, street, alley, court, square, park, sidewalk or any other public grounds or public property within the limits of the city. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 2, 1-17-79; Ord. No. 02-458, § 1, 4-3-02) 
Sec. 6-3. - At-large animals prohibited; exemption. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person owning or having control over, or having custody of, any animal to permit or allow such animal to be at-large upon any private properties, residential or commercial, within the corporate limits of the city. Nothing in this section should be construed to prohibit allowing an animal to be at-large within a fenced area with the permission of the owner of the premises. Provided, however, that city council may establish "no restraint" areas on public property, which shall be appropriately signed and marked with the times and any special conditions of use. Within such "no restraint" areas, owners or persons having custody or control of dogs shall be responsible for the conduct of their dogs, and such dogs must remain under voice control of the owner or person, and the owner or person having custody or control of any dog shall be fully liable for any damage to persons, property, or other dogs. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 3, 1-17-79; Ord. No. 02-458, § 2, 4-3-02) 
Sec. 6-4. - Limit on harbored dogs and cats. 
    There shall be no more than three adult dogs or three adult cats harbored in any one household within the corporate limits of the city. It shall be unlawful for any person to harbor or have control over more than three adult dogs or more than three adult cats within the city, and it shall further be unlawful for any head of a household within the city to permit within his household or upon his residential premises, the harboring of more than three adult dogs or three adult cats. Dogs and cats under the age of six months are excluded from the provisions of this section. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 4, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-5. - Maintaining unvaccinated animals. 
    Any owner who shall maintain or keep an animal more than six months of age on any premises within the corporate limits of the city which has not been vaccinated as required by article III of this chapter, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 19, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-6. - Vaccination required. 
    The owner or custodian (excluding animal shelters) of each domestic dog or cat shall have the animal vaccinated against rabies by four months of age. The animal must receive a booster within the 12-month interval following the initial vaccination. Every domestic dog or cat must be revaccinated against rabies at a minimum of at least once every 36 months with a rabies vaccine licensed by the United States Department of Agriculture. Every dog or cat shall have some means for identifying current vaccination status such as, collar, tag or microchip. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 5, 1-17-79; Ord. No. 03-476, § 1, 5-7-03) 
Sec. 6-7. - Refusal to quarantine or deliver unvaccinated animals a misdemeanor. 
    Any person who shall refuse to voluntarily quarantine his animal upon notification by the animal control officer of the necessity therefor, or who shall refuse to deliver any unvaccinated animal or other animal subject to impoundment under section 6-81, to the animal control officer, or any of his deputies, upon demand for impounding, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 20, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-8. - Misdemeanor for owner to allow animals to be at-large. 
    Any owner, keeper or custodian of an animal who shall allow such animal to be at-large, whether on public or private property, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 21, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-9. - Removal of collar or tag. 
    Any person who shall willfully remove from any animal a collar or tag shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 22, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-10. - Killing or harming of animals prohibited; exception. 
    Any person who shall intentionally kill, cut, maim, harm or injure, in any manner, any dog, cat or other domestic animal or any domestic or wild bird including, but not limited to, ducks or any squirrel within the city, unless such actions are conducted in defense against an attack by such animal upon some person, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 23, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-11. - Inspection of animals. 
    The animal control officer or his authorized deputies shall have the right, at any reasonable time, to inspect any animal to determine if such animal is vaccinated as required by this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 24, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-12. - Dogs or cats of dangerous or vicious propensities. 
(a)	Confinement required. It shall be unlawful for any person owning or keeping a dog or cat to fail to keep such dog or cat confined if such person knows that such dog or cat has dangerous or vicious propensities. For the purposes of this section, the term "confined" shall mean the keeping of a dog or cat in a location from which such dog or cat cannot escape, and into which a member of the general public could not gain access without forcible entry, mechanical assistance or other physical aid, or the permissive act of the owner or occupant. The term "dangerous or vicious propensities" shall mean traits, tendencies or characteristics displayed by a dog or cat that would, upon a chance encounter, place a person of ordinary sensibilities in fear of bodily harm, or would lead a reasonable person to believe that another domestic animal would, upon a chance encounter, be in immediate danger of serious bodily injury or death from such dog or cat. 
(b)	Notification to owner or keeper. Upon receipt of notice that a dog or cat has dangerous or vicious propensities, the animal control officer shall cause notice thereof to be given to the owner or keeper of such dog or cat by mailing same, certified mail, return receipt requested, or by personal delivery, with the officer's return thereon indicating the time and date such notice was delivered. Such notice shall be prima facie evidence that the owner or keeper of such dog or cat has knowledge of the applicable dog's or cat's dangerous or vicious propensities. 
(c)	Appeal. The owner or keeper of a dog or cat who has received a notice that a dog or cat owned or kept by such person has been declared to have dangerous or vicious propensities may appeal such determination to the municipal court of the city. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 18, 1-17-79; Ord. No. 03-468, § 1, 2-19-03; Ord. No. 07-536, § 1, 8-1-07) 
Sec. 6-12.5. - Attacks/remedial procedures. 
(a)	Impoundment. Upon notification that a dog or cat has bitten, scratched or otherwise attacked any person, or mauled or killed any domesticated animal, the animal control officer investigate the allegation, and if he deems there is credible evidence that such event occurred, he shall seize such dog or cat and cause same to be impounded for a period of not less than ten days. Notwithstanding the foregoing, such dog or cat may, at the election of the owner or keeper thereof, be impounded at a certified veterinary facility, subject to written verification and acceptance for impoundment by the veterinarian. All expenses of impoundment, whether at a city impoundment facility or at a private veterinary facility, shall be the sole responsibility of the owner of keeper of such dog or cat. Fees for impoundment at a city facility shall be as established from time to time by the city council of city. After the expiration of ten days of impoundment, the owner or keeper shall be entitled to redeem the impounded dog or cat upon (i) payment of applicable impoundment fees, and (ii) issuance by the animal control officer of a dangerous animal registration certificate. 
(b)	Dangerous animal registration certificate. The animal control officer shall issue a dangerous animal registration certificate upon the filing of an application by the owner or keeper of a dog or cat, which application shall be subject to compliance with the following, and which shall be agreed to by the owner or keeper: 
(1)	The dog or cat subject to the registration certificate shall have a two-inch by two-inch (2" × 2") blaze red warning tag attached to its collar, which shall be kept attached by the owner or keeper for as long as such dog or cat remains in the city. In lieu thereof, such dog or cat may be equipped with a two-inch-wide blaze red collar, which shall be kept attached to the dog or cat for as long as such dog or cat remains in the city. 
(2)	The owner of keeper of such dog or cat shall post signs at the residence where such dog or cat resides, containing letters six inches in height, that contain the words "vicious dog" or "vicious cat," as applicable. Such signs shall be posted at each fence gate, and adjacent to each exterior door to the residence to which the general public has access. 
(3)	The owner or keeper of such dog or cat shall describe the confinement area(s) to be utilized to assure compliance with this section, and which shall be subject to intermittent inspection by the animal control officer. 
(4)	Payment of an application fee of $250.00. 
(5)	Dangerous animal registration certificates shall be valid for a period of one year. It shall be unlawful for the owner or keeper of a dog or cat required to have a dangerous animal registration certificate pursuant to this section to cause or permit such dog or cat to be within the city, whether temporarily or permanently, without having first received a dangerous animal registration certificate for the period in which the dog or cat is situated within the city. 
(c)	Appeal. Notwithstanding the provisions of (a) through (c) above, upon receipt of a complaint that a dog or cat has bitten, scratched or otherwise attacked any person, or mauled or killed any domesticated animal, the owner or keeper thereof shall have the right to appeal such determination to the municipal court. Notice of appeal shall be given not less than 30 days following impoundment of the applicable dog or cat. If the municipal court determines that the dog or cat was improperly impounded, the court shall order the city to reimburse such owner or keeper for any impoundment fees collected, to rescind requirements the dangerous animal registration certificate, and to return the dangerous animal registration certificate application fee. 
(d)	Destruction of dog or cat. If any dog or cat within the city shall bite, scratch, or otherwise attack any person, or maul or kill any domesticated animal, who or which was not at the time trespassing upon the property of the owner or person having control of such animal, the municipal court shall, upon motion of the animal control officer, order and hold a hearing, and if such court shall determine at such hearing that such animal is vicious and dangerous to persons or other domestic animals, the court may order that such animal be kept muzzled, or that such animal be kept within an enclosure, or that such animal be delivered to the animal control officer and destroyed." 
(Ord. No. 07-536, § 1, 8-1-07) 
Sec. 6-13. - Feeding wild animals. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to feed a wild animal within the city. 
(b)	The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Feed means providing food for a wild animal, including the leaving of food, unattended, at a location available to wild animals. 
    Wild animal means a nondomesticated animal which is at large, or otherwise not within the control of an owner. The term "wild animal" shall not include bird of wildfowl of any type. 
(Ord. No. 98-395, § 2, 5-6-98) 
Secs. 6-14-6-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - IMPOUNDMENT 

Sec. 6-41. - Seizure of at-large animals. 
    It shall be the duty of the animal control officer or any of his deputies, while on duty, to seize and impound, subject to the provisions of this chapter, all animals found at-large upon any public street, alley, court, square, park, sidewalk or any other public property within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 6, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-42. - Seizure of untagged dogs or cats. 
    It shall be the duty of the animal control officer or any of his deputies while on duty to seize and impound, subject to the provisions of this chapter, all dogs and cats not wearing the tag required under section 6-6, found at-large upon any vacant unfenced lot, tract or parcel of land within the corporate limits of the city. Such animal control officer or deputy is hereby authorized to enter upon any vacant unfenced lot, tract or parcel of land for the purpose of seizing and impounding any such dog or any such cat running at-large thereon. Nothing in this section should be construed as authority to enter private residential premises without the permission of the owner. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 7, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-43. - Citizen seizure. 
(a)	Any person may take up and deliver to the animal control officer any animal which the animal control officer is, by the provisions of this chapter, required to impound. 
(b)	Any animal found trespassing or at-large upon any private property may be taken up by the owner of such property and delivered to the animal control officer. Every person other than the animal control officer or his deputies that takes up any animal under the provisions of this chapter, shall immediately thereafter give notice to the animal control officer, and every such person, or any person in whose custody such animal may in the meantime be placed, shall deliver such animal to the animal control officer without fee or charge. The animal control officer shall thereupon proceed in his duties as though such animal had been found at-large and impounded by him. When animals are found at-large and their ownership is known to the animal control officer or his deputies, such animals need not be impounded, but the officer may, in his discretion, cite the owners of such animals to appear in municipal court to answer charges of violation of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 115, §§ 8, 9, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-44. - Registry required. 
    The animal control officer or his deputies upon receiving any animal shall make a complete registry, entering the breed, color and sex of such animal and the place and time of taking into custody. If wearing the tag required under section 6-6, he shall enter the name and address of the owner and the number of the tag. Tagged animals shall be kept separated from untagged animals. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 10, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-45. - Notice of impounding. 
    As soon as possible after any animal has been delivered to the animal control officer of the city, it shall be his duty to post a notice at the city office describing each of such animals, whether bearing a veterinarian tag or not, and giving the number of the tag and the name of the person owning the animal in each case where the animal bears a tag. In case the animal bears a tag, then in addition to posting notice as required in this section, it shall be the duty of the animal control officer to notify the person to whom such tag was issued, by letter, postal card or telephone. The mailing of such letter or postal card shall be deemed sufficient notice whether the person addressed shall receive the same or not. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 11, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-46. - Redemption; fee. 
    The owner of any untagged animal impounded may redeem such animal at any time prior to disposition or destruction by having such animal duly tagged, vaccinated against rabies, and the payment of a fee as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the city secretary. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 12, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-47. - Period of impoundment-Tagged animals; notice to owner; disposition of unclaimed animals. 
    It shall be the duty of the animal control officer to keep all unclaimed animals wearing a veterinarian's tag for a period of ten days from the date of the impounding. If at the expiration of such period of time and after reasonable efforts to notify the owner such animal has not been redeemed by the owner, the city secretary shall be notified; and if the animal is not redeemed within three days after such notice, on the direction of the city secretary it shall be disposed of or destroyed. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 13, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-48. - Same-Untagged animals; notice to owner; disposition of unclaimed animals. 
    It shall be the duty of the animal control officer to keep all unclaimed untagged animals for a period of five days. If, at the expiration of such period of time, and after reasonable efforts to notify the owner, if determinable, such animal has not been redeemed, the city secretary shall be notified; and if the animal is not redeemed within three days after such notice, on the direction of the city secretary it shall be destroyed or disposed of as provided in this article. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 14, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-49. - Destruction of unclaimed animals; alternative. 
    All animals impounded and not redeemed or reclaimed after the period of time for redemption has expired, shall forthwith without further notice be destroyed in the most practicable humane manner by the animal control officer; provided, however, that in lieu of destruction of such animal by the animal control officer, such officer is authorized to donate such animals to the Society for Prevention of Cruelty to Animals. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 15, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-50. - Recordkeeping; disposition of money collected. 
    The animal control officer shall keep necessary records as are required to show in detail the disposition of all animals impounded and the money collected by him, and such other records as are required by the city secretary. All money collected shall be delivered to the city secretary, who will deposit such funds in the general fund. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 16, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-51. - Reports. 
    The animal control officer shall file such reports as are required by the city secretary. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 17, 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-52. - Pound established; fees. 
    The city council shall adopt appropriate resolutions designating a city pound and/or person to receive and impound dogs and other animals seized within the limits of the city, and the city council hereby reserves the right to choose to contract for these services. The location of such pound shall be at such place within or without the city as the city council may determine appropriate. The council additionally may, by appropriate resolution, provide for fees to be paid by the owners of such animals upon their reclamation from the city pound, and may authorize the mayor to enter into a contract to accomplish the purposes of any such resolutions passed, including a contract for the disposition of animals remaining unclaimed in the city pound and payment to the pound or person acting as manager thereof of reasonable fees for the disposition of unclaimed animals in accordance with section 6-49. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 27, 1-17-79) 
Secs. 6-53-6-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - RABIES CONTROL 

Sec. 6-81. - Biting incidents; reports; quarantine. 
    Every animal which bites a person shall be promptly reported to the animal control officer and shall thereupon be securely quarantined at the direction of the animal control officer for a period of ten days and shall not be released from such quarantine except by written permission of the animal control officer. Such quarantine may be conducted on the premises of the owner, if the owner of the animal can display a valid rabies vaccination certificate issued within the 12-month through 36-month period next preceding the biting incident, or, at owner's option and expense, at the shelter designated as the city pound or, at the owner's option and expense, in a veterinary hospital of his choice. In the case of stray animals, or in the cases of animals whose ownership is unknown such quarantine shall be at the shelter designated as the city pound. However, owners of animals for which no valid rabies vaccination certificate issued within the 12-month through 36-month period next preceding the biting incident can be displayed or presented shall have their animal quarantined at a veterinary hospital of their choice at such owner's expense. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 25(a), 1-17-79; Ord. No. 03-476, § 2, 5-7-03) 
Sec. 6-82. - Surrender of animal for quarantine; expenses. 
    The owner, upon demand made by the animal control officer, shall forthwith surrender any animal which is suspected of having been exposed to rabies, for supervised quarantine, which expense shall be borne by the owner, and may be reclaimed by the owner if adjudged free of rabies, upon payment of fees as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the city secretary and upon compliance with licensing provisions as set forth in this article. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 25(b), 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-83. - Pathological examination of dead animal's head. 
    When an animal under quarantine has been diagnosed as being rabid, or suspected by a licensed veterinarian as being rabid, and dies while under such observation, the animal control officer shall immediately send the head of such animal to the state health department for pathological examination, and shall notify the city health officer of reports of human contacts, and the diagnosis made of the suspected animal. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 25(c), 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-84. - City-wide quarantine upon positive diagnosis. 
    When the report of the state health department or a laboratory examination approved by the health department gives a positive diagnosis of rabies, the animal control officer may recommend to the village health officer a city-wide quarantine for a period of 30 days, and, upon the invoking of such quarantine, no animal shall be taken into the streets or permitted to be in the streets during such period of quarantine. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 25(d), 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-85. - Animals bitten by animals; procedures. 
    During such period of rabies quarantine as mentioned in this article, every animal bitten by an animal adjudged to be rabid shall, at the owner's option and expense, be treated for rabies infection by a licensed veterinarian, or held under six months quarantine by the owner in the same manner that other animals that are quarantined under this article, or if such owner will not comply with either of the latter provisions, such animal shall be impounded and may be destroyed. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 25(e), 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-86. - Extension of quarantine period. 
    If there are additional positive cases of rabies occurring during the period of quarantine, such period of quarantine may be extended by the city health officer for an additional reasonable period of time. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 25(f), 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-87. - Killing or disposal of rabid animal. 
    No person shall kill, or cause to be killed, any rabid animal, or dispose of by burial, incineration or other means, any animal suspected of having been exposed to rabies, or any animal having bitten a human, except as provided in this article, nor remove such animal from the city limits without written permission from the animal control officer or chief of police. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 25(g), 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-88. - Surrender of carcass of rabid animal. 
    The carcass of any dead animal exposed to rabies shall upon demand be surrendered to the animal control officer or chief of police. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 25(h), 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-89. - Direction of disposition by city authorities. 
    The animal control officer or chief of police shall direct the disposition of any animal found to be infected with rabies. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 25(i), 1-17-79) 
Sec. 6-90. - Failure or refusal to surrender animal for quarantine or destruction. 
    No person shall fail or refuse to surrender any animal for quarantine or destruction as required in this article when demand is made therefor by the animal control officer or chief of police. 
(Ord. No. 115, § 25(j), 1-17-79) 
Chapters 7-9 - RESERVED 
Chapter 10 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 10-1. - Fees. 
    The city council may by resolution establish the fees and charges for building, plumbing, mechanical, electrical work and other permits and inspections. Permit fees, inspections fees and any other fee or charge which may be imposed or required under the provisions of any of the construction and technical codes adopted by this chapter shall be as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the city secretary. 
(Ord. No. 10-595, § 1, 6-2-2010; Ord. No. 12-623, § 1, 9-5-2012) 
Sec. 10-2. - Registration requirements for contractors. 
    The following requirements shall be applicable to all mechanical, plumbing, electrical, and general contractors performing work within the city: 
(1)	Administrative fee. All contractors shall be required to register with the city and pay, with the exception of plumbers licensed under Texas Occupations Code chapter 1301, an annual administrative fee for such registration prior to undertaking work within the city limits. The registration fee shall be an amount established by city council in the schedule of fees on file with the city secretary. "Contractor" shall be defined as a person, other than a homeowner, who is required to obtain a permit from the city before beginning construction or repair work on any residence or commercial establishment within the city limits. All contractors shall complete a registration form provided by the city and provide copies of all the documents listed below, as well as any other documentation requested by the city. Failure to provide this information, or update same, shall constitute cause for revocation of such registration. 
(2)	Insurance. All contractors shall be required to present proof of liability insurance in the minimum amount of $300,000.00 at the time of registration with the city. Proof of workman's compensation insurance shall not be required. 
(3)	License. The following specific licenses shall be required of each type of contractor, each of which shall be issued by, and in accordance with, the laws of the State of Texas: 
a.	Mechanical-Mechanical license. 
b.	Plumbing-Plumbers' license. 
c.	Electrical-Master electrician's license. 
d.	General-No license required. 
(Ord. No. 02-457, § 1, 3-20-02; Ord. No. 10-595, § 1, 6-2-2010; Ord. No. 12-623, § 1, 9-5-2012) 
Sec. 10-3. - Building department. 
    The city will maintain a building department to administer and enforce building codes, zoning regulations, flood ordinance regulations, and related matters as adopted by the city. 
(1)	The building department will be operated by the building official under the direct supervision of the mayor. Other city employees and contractors may participate in building department matters. City council will provide guidance and direction to the mayor on building department matters. 
(2)	The building department will issue building permits, conduct inspections, and engage in other activities required to ensure that construction, building, and remodeling work on property within the city's jurisdiction is completed in accordance with all applicable building codes, zoning regulations, flood ordinance, and similar requirements. 
(3)	The city will assess to permittees and others using building department services, fees in accordance with the current fee schedule. 
(Ord. No. 11-610, § 3, 8-3-2011) 
Sec. 10-4. - Building official. 
    The city establishes the position of Building Official of the City of Taylor Lake Village. 
(1)	The building official will be responsible for implementing the functions of the building department and must be qualified to conduct the relevant duties as outlined in the building official job description. 
(2)	The engagement term, tenure, compensation, and duties of the building official will be governed by building official contract currently in effect. 
(Ord. No. 11-610, § 3, 8-3-2011) 
Sec. 10-5. - Additional building department service providers. 
    As appropriate and as determined by city council, the city may engage qualified outside service providers to support and augment the services of the building department. 
(1)	Such providers may include building inspectors, plan reviewers, engineers, or other specialties. 
(2)	Qualified providers must be approved and accepted by city council prior to their engagement and use for city-related work. 
(3)	Costs, including any associated administrative fees, for services rendered by persons classified as additional building department service providers must be borne by the building permittee requesting or requiring an outside service provider. 
(Ord. No. 11-610, § 3, 8-3-2011) 
Sec. 10-6. - Severability. 
    In the event any clause, phrase, provision, sentence, or part of this article or the application of the same to any person or circumstance shall for any reason be adjudged invalid or held unconstitutional by a court of competent jurisdiction, it shall not affect, impair, or invalidate this article as a whole or any part or provision hereof other than the part declared to be invalid or unconstitutional; and the City Council of the City of Taylor Lake Village, Texas, declares that it would have passed each and every part of the same notwithstanding the omission of any such part thus declared to be invalid or unconstitutional, whether there be one or more parts. 
(Ord. No. 11-610, § 3, 8-3-2011) 
Secs. 10-7-10-20. - Reserved.

Sec. 10-31. - 2012 Edition of International Code Council Codes (I-Codes) and the latest National Electrical Code. 
(a)	Adoption. The following codes: 
  2012 International Building Code 
  2012 International Residential Code for One- and Two-Family Dwellings 
  2012 International Mechanical Code 
  2012 International Plumbing Code (includes the 2012 IPSDC) 
  2012 International Fire Code 
  2012 International Fuel Gas Code 
  2012 International Energy Conservation Code 
  2012 International Existing Building Code 
  2012 International Wildland-Urban Interface Code 
  2012 ICC Performance Code for Buildings and Facilities 
  2012 International Property Maintenance Code 
  2012 International Zoning Code 
  2012 International Private Sewage Disposal Code 
  2012 International Green Construction Code(tm) (IgCC(tm)) 
  2012 International Swimming Pool and Spa Code(tm) (ISPSC(tm)) 
  2011 National Electrical Code (NFPA 70) 
are hereby adopted as the "Building Code" of the City of Taylor Lake Village, as published by the International Code Council, Inc. 
(b)	Local amendments. Local amendments to the code are shown in Exhibit A, attached hereto. 
(c)	Most stringent standard to apply. In any specific case, where sections of the code, or any existing city ordinance that adopts a professionally recognized building code or construction standard, specify different materials, methods of construction, or other requirements, the most restrictive standard shall govern. Where there is a conflict between a general requirement and a specific requirement, the specific requirement shall be applicable. 
(d)	Future amendments. Future amendments of the model codes (not including clarifications or technical notices of any type) are not adopted by this section, and must be subsequently approved and adopted by the city council. 
(e)	Effect of codes. The adoption of the model codes by the city shall not be construed to relieve or lessen the responsibility of any person owning, operating, or controlling any building or structure for any damages to persons or property caused by defects, nor shall the city council, the city, its agents or representatives assume any such liability by reason of these regulations or the inspections authorized by this code or any permits or certificates issued under the codes. 
(f)	Penalty. Any person, corporation, or entity who or which violates any provision of this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be fined in an amount not to exceed $2,000.00. Each day in which any violation shall occur, or each occurrence of any violation, shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 95-362, § 1, 7-19-95; Ord. No. 04-491, §§ 1-6, 2-18-04; Ord. No. 12-623, §§ 2-6, 9-5-2012)
