ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 26-1-26-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - BURGLAR ALARM SYSTEMS[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Law enforcement, ch. 38. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 26-31. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Alarm system means, individually or collectively, a burglar alarm protection service, fire alarm protection service, burglar alarm system or fire alarm system; not to include simple smoke alarm systems not connected to alarm service organizations or that cannot be heard outside of the building. 
    Burglar alarm protection service means any service whereby the person providing such service employs electronic or mechanical means to detect the unlawful entry or attempted unlawful entry into premises within the city, the report of which is then transmitted to the police department of the city or is in any manner connected with the communication system of the police department of the city. 
    Burglar alarm system means a local protective signaling system so designed and operated that both the equipment for detecting unlawful entry and the equipment for sounding a warning thereof by bell, horn, siren or other means are located on the particular premises being protected, and the warning sound is designed to be heard or capable of being heard outside the premises at a distance of 50 feet from such premises. 
    False alarm means the activation of any alarm system which was not the result of an emergency or threat of emergency of the kind for which the burglar alarm protection service, fire alarm protection service, burglar alarm system or fire alarm system was designed to give notice. 
    Fire alarm protection service means any service whereby the person providing such service employs electronic or mechanical means to detect the presence of fire on any premises in the city, the report of which is then transmitted to the police department or fire department of the city, or is in any manner connected with the fire alarm communication system of the police department or fire department of the city. 
    Fire alarm system means a local protective signaling system so designed and operated that both the equipment for detecting fire and the equipment for sounding a warning thereof by bell, horn, siren or other means are located on the particular premises being protected, and the warning sound is designed to be heard or capable of being heard outside the premises at a distance of 50 feet from such premises. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 2, 2-1-89) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 26-32. - Response by police and fire department; charges for false alarms. 
    The police department and/or fire department of the city will respond to proper notification of activation of an alarm system without charge except: Fees as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the city secretary shall be charged for each response by the police department and/or fire department to notification of activation of an alarm system in excess of three fire alarms and five burglar alarms from the same site of an alarm system within the previous 12-month period; provided, however, that no fee will be charged for a response to notification of the activation of an alarm system if the registration certificate holder shows that the activation was not a false alarm, and any response by the police department and/or fire department to notification of the activation of an alarm system will not be included in determining the fees referred to in this section if the registration certificate holder shows that such was not a false alarm. For purposes of determining the fees set out in this section, the burden shall be on the owner of the alarm system to prove that the activation of the alarm system was not a false alarm. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 12, 2-1-89; Ord. No. 01-441, § 12, 6-20-01) 
Sec. 26-33. - Shutoff requirements. 
(a)	Shutoff devices required. It shall be unlawful for any person to install, cause to be installed or permit the installation of any burglar alarm system or fire alarm system within the city which is not equipped with a shutoff device. For the purposes of this section a shutoff device shall mean an automatic device which causes the audible signal of the alarm to shut off and discontinue after a period of time not to exceed 15 minutes from the time of the commencement of the emission of such audible signal. It shall be unlawful for any person to operate, cause to be operated, or permit the operation of a burglar alarm system or fire alarm system within the city which is not equipped with a shutoff device designed and adjusted to discontinue the emission of the audible signal of such alarm within 15 minutes from the time of the commencement of the emission of such audible signal. 
(b)	Installation of automatic dialing devices. It shall be unlawful for any person to install, cause to be installed or permit the installation of any alarm system within the city equipped with an automatic dialing device unless such device is equipped with a means to automatically disconnect and discontinue the transmittal of the prerecorded message after the message has been communicated to the police department or fire department. For the purposes of this section, an automatic dialing device is any device connected to any alarm system which automatically sends a prerecorded message indicating the activation of the alarm system to the police department or fire department. 
(c)	Operation of automatic dialing device. It shall be unlawful for any person to operate, cause to be operated or permit the operation of an alarm system within the city equipped with an automatic dialing device unless such device is equipped with a means to automatically disconnect and discontinue the transmittal of the prerecorded message after such message has been communicated to the police department or fire department. 
(d)	Sprinkler system exception. Notwithstanding any other provision of this article to the contrary, the provisions of subsections (a), (b) and (c) of this section shall not apply to any fire alarm system or fire alarm protection service, or the erection, operation or maintenance thereof, if such system or service activates, operates or deactivates a sprinkler system. For the purposes of this subsection, the term "sprinkler system" shall mean a sprinkler system for fire protection purposes and is an integrated system of underground and overhead piping designed in accordance with fire protection engineering standards. The installation includes a water supply, such as a gravity tank, fire pump, reservoir or pressure tank and/or connection by underground piping to a city main. The portion of the sprinkler system above the ground is a network of specially sized or hydraulically designed piping installed in a building, structure or area, generally overhead, and to which sprinklers are connected in a systematic pattern. The system includes a controlling valve and a device for activating an alarm when the system is in operation. The system is usually activated by heat from a fire and discharges water over the fire area. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 13, 2-1-89) 
Sec. 26-34. - Activation of alarm system for purposes other than emergency prohibited; exception. 
    No person shall intentionally activate an alarm system for any purpose other than an emergency or threat of emergency of the kind for which the alarm system was designed to give notice; provided, however, that it shall be an affirmative defense to prosecution under this section that the alarm system was activated solely for the purpose of testing the alarm system, and the person who tested the alarm system took reasonable precautions to avoid any request being made to the police department or fire department to respond to such alarm. This section shall not apply to conduct which is in violation of V.T.C.A., Penal Code § 42.06. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 14, 2-1-89) 
Sec. 26-35. - Confidential information. 
    All information received by the city as required by this article shall be deemed confidential and not a matter of public record. No such information shall be released to any person other than necessary city administrative, police and fire personnel, unless specifically authorized, in writing, by the person in control of the property about which such information is related. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 15, 2-1-89) 
Sec. 26-36. - Compliance with article provisions. 
    Each holder of a registration certificate, and each person having control over property on which an alarm system is installed, has an affirmative duty to comply with all provisions of this article. It shall not be a defense to prosecution of such a person that he was acting without culpable mental state. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 16, 2-1-89) 
Secs. 26-37-26-55. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - REGISTRATION 

Sec. 26-56. - Application for registration of burglar or fire alarm system. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to install, cause to be installed, or permit the installation of a burglar alarm system or fire alarm system within the city without filing a registration of such system with the city secretary. Applications for registration shall be available at the city office, and each application shall comply with section 26-59; provided, however, that if the burglar alarm system or fire alarm system is used in conjunction or in combination with a burglar alarm protection service or fire alarm protection service, then, in such event, the application shall also comply with section 26-60. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 3, 2-1-89) 
Sec. 26-58. - Operation of system or protection service without registration. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or permit the operation of a burglar alarm system, fire alarm system, burglar alarm protection service or fire alarm protection service on property over which such person has control, unless such person has registered such burglar alarm system, fire alarm system, burglar alarm protection service or fire alarm protection service. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 5, 2-1-89) 
Sec. 26-59. - Contents of application for registry of burglar or fire alarm systems. 
    Application for registration of a burglar alarm system or fire alarm system shall be made by a person having control over the property on which the burglar alarm system or fire alarm system is to be installed and operated or is being operated. Applications shall be filed with the city secretary and shall contain the following: 
(1)	The street address of the property on which the alarm system is installed; 
(2)	The name and telephone number of the occupant of the premises on which the alarm system is installed; 
(3)	If an occupant is not the owner, the name, address and telephone number of the owner of the property on which the alarm system is installed; 
(4)	The name, address and telephone number of two persons to be notified if the alarm system is activated. The names of the persons shall be given only if they are able and have agreed to: 
a.	Receive notification at any time; 
b.	Come to the site of the alarm system within one hour after receiving a request from a member of the police department; and 
c.	Grant access to the site of the alarm system and to deactivate the alarm if such becomes necessary; or 
(5)	The name, address and telephone number of the person to be notified to render service or repairs during any hour of the day or night that the alarm system sounds. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 6, 2-1-89) 
Sec. 26-60. - Contents of application for registry of burglar or fire alarm protection service. 
    Applications for registration of a burglar alarm protection service and any included burglar alarm system, or fire alarm protection service and any included fire alarm system shall be made by a person having control over the property on which the alarm system is to be installed and operated or is being operated. Applications shall be filed with the city secretary and shall contain the following: 
(1)	The street address of the property on which the alarm system is installed; 
(2)	The name and telephone number of the occupant of the premises on which the alarm system is installed; 
(3)	If an occupant is not the owner, the name, address and telephone number of the owner of the property on which the alarm system is installed; 
(4)	The name, address and telephone number of the person providing the burglar alarm protection service or fire alarm protection service; 
(5)	If a burglar alarm protection service includes a burglar alarm system or if a fire alarm protection service includes a fire alarm system, the information specified in subsection 26-59(4) and (5). 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 7, 2-1-89) 
Sec. 26-61. - Validity period; renewal. 
    Each registration issued in accordance with this article shall be valid for a period of 12 months from the date it is issued. The registration shall be renewed in accordance with sections 26-59 and 26-60. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 8, 2-1-89) 
Sec. 26-62. - Fees. 
    The fee for registration, pursuant to this article, shall be as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the city secretary. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 9, 2-1-89) 
Sec. 26-63. - Personal to applicant; transferral. 
    Each registration pursuant to this article shall be personal to the applicant and is not transferable. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 10, 2-1-89) 
Sec. 26-64. - Issuance of certificate; display; inspection. 
    Copies of registration certificates shall be issued by the city secretary at the time a valid application is made. The holder of the registration certificate shall keep such certificate at the location of the premises being protected and shall produce such permit for inspection upon the request of any member of the police department or fire department. 
(Ord. No. 89-286, § 11, 2-1-89) 
Chapters 27-29 - RESERVED 
Chapter 30 - ENVIRONMENT[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Animals, ch. 6; buildings and building regulations, ch. 10; substandard buildings, § 10-66 et seq.; floods, ch. 34; natural resources, ch. 42; planning and zoning, ch. 54; solid waste, ch. 58; subdivisions, ch. 66; waterways, ch. 78; zoning, app. A. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 30-1. - Deposit of refuse in Taylor Bayou or Taylor Lake. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to deposit in Taylor Bayou or Taylor Lake the carcass of any dead animal, tin cans, discarded buckets or pails, garbage, paper, ashes, earth or refuse of any character, or any other articles which might pollute the water, obstruct the flow or interfere with navigation. 
(Ord. No. 18, § 1, 12-22-62) 
Cross reference- Solid waste, ch. 58. 
Secs. 30-2-30-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - JUNK VEHICLES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Traffic and vehicles, ch. 74. 

Sec. 30-31. - Definitions. 
    Any word not specifically defined in this section shall have the same meaning as that word has under Vernon's Ann. Civ. St. art. 4477-9A, § 5.01. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Antique auto means a passenger car or truck that is at least 35 years old. 
    Collector means the owner of one or more antique or special interest vehicles who collects, purchases, acquires, trades or disposes of special interest or antique vehicles or parts of them for personal use in order to restore, preserve and maintain an antique or special interest vehicle for historic interest. 
    Demolisher means a person or entity whose business is to convert a motor vehicle into processed scrap or scrap metal or to otherwise wreck or dismantle a motor vehicle. 
    Junk vehicle means any motor vehicle, as defined in Vernon's Ann. Civ. St. art. 6701d-11, § 1, as amended, which is: 
(1)	Inoperative and which does not have lawfully affixed thereto either an unexpired license plate or plates or a valid motor vehicle safety inspection certificate and which is wrecked, dismantled, partially dismantled or discarded; or 
(2)	Has remained inoperable for more than 72 consecutive hours if on public property and 30 consecutive days if on private property. 
    Special interest vehicle means a motor vehicle of any age that has not been altered or modified from original manufacturer's specifications and, because of its historic interest, is being preserved by hobbyists. 
(Ord. No. 89-299, § 1, 9-14-89; Ord. No. 01-443, § 1, 5-17-00) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 30-32. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person who maintains a nuisance shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-9. In addition, upon conviction, the court shall order removal and abatement of the nuisance, which order may be enforced by any means authorized by the laws of the state. 
(Ord. No. 89-299, § 6, 9-14-89) 
Sec. 30-33. - Declared public nuisance. 
    A junked vehicle that is located in any place where it is visible from a public place or public right-of-way or is detrimental to the safety and welfare of the general public, tends to reduce the value of private property, invites vandalism, creates fire hazards, constitutes an attractive nuisance creating a hazard to the health and safety of minors and is detrimental to the economic welfare of the city by producing urban blight which is adverse to the maintenance and continuing development of the city, and such vehicles are hereby declared to be a public nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 89-299, § 2, 9-14-89; Ord. No. 09-567, § 1.A, 1-7-09) 
Sec. 30-34. - Administration; authority to enforce article provisions. 
    Whenever it shall be determined by the chief of police or any full-time, salaried, city officer acting under his direction, that a junked vehicle or part thereof, is located in a place where it is visible from a public place or public right-of-way, or constitutes a public nuisance by definition under section 30-33: 
(1)	For a nuisance on private property, the chief of police shall give not less than ten days' notice stating the nature of the public nuisance on private property, that it must be removed and abated within ten days, and that a request for a hearing must be made before expiration of the ten-day period. The notice shall be mailed, by certified mail, with a five-day return requested, to the owner or occupant of the private premises on which the public nuisance exists. If the notice is returned undelivered by the United States post office, official action to abate the nuisance shall be continued to a date not less than ten days after the date of the return. In addition, notice shall be given to the last registered owner of such vehicle, if determinable. 
(2)	For a nuisance on public property, the chief of police shall give not less than ten days' notice, stating the nature of the public nuisance on public property or on a public right-of-way, that the nuisance must be removed and abated within ten days, and that a request for a hearing must be made before the expiration of the ten-day period. The notice shall be mailed, by certified mail, with a five-day return requested, to the owner or occupant of the premises adjacent to the public right-of-way on which the public nuisance exists and to the last known registered owner, if determinable. If the notice is returned undelivered by the United States post office, official action to abate the nuisance shall be continued to a date not less than ten days after the date of the return. 
(3)	When a public hearing is requested, as provided in this section, by the owner or occupant of the premises whereupon such public nuisance exists or the owner of such vehicle, it shall be held before the mayor at the city hall, at a time to be set by such official, but not less than ten days after services of notice to abate the nuisance. Following the hearing, if a public nuisance is found by the mayor to exist, he shall enter an order requiring the removal of the vehicle, or part thereof, and shall state a time for such removal to be accomplished, which in no event shall exceed ten days from the date of hearing. The order shall include a description of the vehicle, or part thereof, and the correct identification number and license number of the vehicle, if available at the site thereof. After removal of any junked vehicle under this article, it shall not thereafter be reconstructed or made operable. 
(4)	When the junked vehicle, or part thereof, remains on the property after ordered removed, as provided by this article, the mayor may cause the vehicle to be removed and sold for the best price obtainable to a scrap yard or demolisher. All sums so raised shall be turned over to the city secretary for deposit in general fund of the city. 
(5)	If the nuisance is not removed and abated and a hearing is not requested within the ten-day period provided in subsections (1) or (2) of this section, then a nuisance complaint shall be filed in the appropriate court. 
(Ord. No. 89-299, § 3, 9-14-89; Ord. No. 09-567, § 1.B, 1-7-09) 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2. 
Sec. 30-35. - Notice to the department of highways and public transportation. 
    Within five days after the date of the removal, notice shall be given to the department of highways and public transportation, identifying the vehicle, or part thereof. 
(Ord. No. 89-299, § 5, 9-14-89) 
Sec. 30-36. - Conflict with state law provisions concerning abandoned motor vehicles. 
    Nothing in this article shall be construed to conflict with procedures set forth for dealing with abandoned motor vehicles. 
(Ord. No. 89-299, § 7, 9-14-89) 
Sec. 30-37. - Exceptions to article provisions. 
    The provisions of this article shall not apply to: 
(1)	A vehicle or part thereof which is completely enclosed within a building in a lawful manner where it is not visible from the street or other public property; 
(2)	A vehicle or part thereof which is stored or parked in a lawful manner on private property if the vehicle and outdoor storage area are maintained in a manner so that they do not constitute a health hazard or fire hazard and also must be screened form ordinary public view by means of a fence, rapidly growing trees, shrubbery or other appropriate means. 
(Ord. No. 89-299, § 8, 9-14-89; Ord. No. 09-567, § 1.C, 1-7-09) 
Secs. 30-38-30-65. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - NOISE CONTROL 

Sec. 30-66. - Prohibited acts-Generally. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to make, continue or cause to be made or continued any loud, unnecessary or unusual noise or any noise which either annoys, disturbs, injures or endangers the comfort, repose, health, peace, safety or welfare of others within the limits of the city, unless the making and continuing of the noise is necessary for the protection or preservation of property or of the health, safety, life or limb of some person. 
(Ord. No. 79-126, § 1, 10-3-79) 
Sec. 30-67. - Same-Enumeration. 
    The acts enumerated in this article are declared to be loud, disturbing and unnecessary noises in violation of this section, but such enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive: 
(1)	Sirens, whistles or gongs on vehicles. It shall be unlawful for any person to carry or to use upon any vehicle other than police or fire department vehicles or other emergency vehicles, any gong or siren similar to that used on ambulances or vehicles of the police and fire department. 
(2)	Mufflers on engines. No person shall operate a gasoline engine or any similar engine of any kind unless such engine shall be equipped with an exhaust muffler in effective working condition, which muffler shall be used whenever the engine is in operation so that there will be no excessive or unusual noise or the engine shall be so constructed or designed that the noise is deadened as if such engine were equipped with a muffler. No person shall operate a motor vehicle upon any street unless such motor vehicle is equipped with a muffler at all times in good working order sufficient to prevent excessive or unusual noise. 
(3)	Noisy vehicles generally. It shall be unlawful to use any automobile, motorcycle or other vehicle out of repair or so loud or in such a manner as to create any loud or noisy grating, grinding, rattling or other noise. 
(4)	Playing of radios, phonographs, other sound producing or reproducing devices generally. It shall be unlawful for any person to use, operate or permit to be played, used or operated any radio receiving set, television set, musical instrument, phonograph or other machine or device for the producing or reproducing of sound in such a manner as to disturb the peace, quiet and comfort of the neighboring inhabitants, or at any time with louder volume that is necessary for convenient hearing for persons who are in the room, vehicle or chamber in which such machine or device is operated and who are voluntary listeners thereto. 
(5)	Building operations and lawn maintenance at night. It shall be unlawful for any person in conducting any building operations or lawn maintenance between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. to operate or use offensive lawn equipment or any piledriver, steam shovel, pneumatic hammer, derrick, steam or electric hoist or other apparatus, the use of which is at the time loud or unusually noisy, except in case of emergency. On Saturdays, Sundays and holidays, the hours shall be extended to between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 8:00 a.m. 
(6)	Noise near school, church, court or hospital. The creation of any excessive noise on any street adjacent to any school, institution of learning, church or court while the same is in use, or adjacent to any hospital, which unreasonably interferes with the workings of such institutions, or which disturbs or unduly annoys patients in the hospital, is hereby prohibited, provided that conspicuous signs are displayed in such streets indicating that the same is a school, hospital, church or court street. 
(7)	Barking dogs. It shall be unlawful for any person to own, keep, have in his possession or harbor any dog or other animal or fowl which by frequent howling, yelping, barking or otherwise causes annoyance or disturbance to persons in the neighborhood. 
(Ord. No. 79-126, § 1, 10-3-79; Ord. No. 12-620, § 1, 5-2-2012) 
Secs. 30-68-30-100. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - NUISANCES 

Sec. 30-101. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Nuisance means whatever is dangerous to life or health, and whatever renders the ground, the water, the air or any food or drink unhealthy and a hazard to life or health. 
(Ord. No. 79-125, § 1, 9-19-79) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 30-102. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished according to the provisions of section 1-9. If the owner or occupant of any lot or premises shall be a corporation and shall violate any provision of this article, the president, vice-president, secretary or treasurer of such corporation, or any manager, agent or employee of such corporation, shall also be severally liable for any penalty. 
(Ord. No. 79-125, § 5, 9-19-79; Ord. No. 84-225, § 1, 10-17-84) 
Sec. 30-103. - Enumeration. 
    The following, without limiting the definitions in section 30-101, are specifically declared to be public nuisances, and as such are liable to be abated, and the person guilty of causing, permitting or suffering any such nuisance then upon his premises or in any building occupied or controlled by him or in or upon any street, alley, sidewalk or gutter immediately adjacent to such premises shall be deemed in violation of this article: 
(1)	The accumulation of stagnant water; 
(2)	The accumulation of carrion, filth or other impure or unwholesome matter; 
(3)	Weeds which have grown to a height of more than 12 inches, or any other rubbish, brush or other unsightly, objectionable or unsanitary matter. 
(4)	Inoperable or damaged boats and related debris, including but not limited to, boats or related marine material which are placed in the waterways located within the city limits, and which may become partially or wholly submerged, thereby constituting a danger to the public health, safety and welfare. 
(5)	Plant growth that encroaches on or over any sidewalk, beyond any curb line, or over the edge of the pavement. Every owner, tenant, or occupant of the premises abutting or adjoining any public right of way shall edge, trim or remove any grass, trees, shrubbery, or plant growth so that such vegetation does not encroach on or over any sidewalk, beyond any curb line, or over the edge of the pavement. 
(6)	Plant material or vegetation allowed to overhang or encroach onto the sidewalk, curb, or street in such a manner as to create a hazard to pedestrians or bicyclists or to look unsightly. It shall be unlawful for any owner, tenant, or occupant of any premises to allow or permit any plant material or vegetation to overhang or encroach onto the sidewalk, curb, or street on or immediately adjacent to such premises in such a manner as to create a hazard to pedestrians or bicyclists, or to look unsightly. 
(Ord. No. 79-125, § 2, 9-19-79; Ord. No. 03-469, § 1, 2-19-03; Ord. No. 16-666, § 1, 10-15-16) 
Sec. 30-104. - Abatement by city. 
    If any person who owns any lot or building within the city does not abate a nuisance as described in this article within seven days after notice to such person, as provided in section 30-105, the city may do or cause to be done that which will abate the nuisance, and may pay the expense therefore, and charge such expenses incurred in doing such work or having such work done or improvements made to the person who owns such lot or building. If such work is done or improvements made at the expense of the city, such expense shall be assessed on the real property upon which such expense was incurred as provided in section 30-106. 
(Ord. No. 81-173, § 1(A), 9-2-81; Ord. No. 00-426, § 1, 5-17-00) 
Sec. 30-105. - Dissemination of notice. 
(a)	The notice required in section 30-104 shall be given: 
(1)	Personally to the owner in writing; 
(2)	By letter addressed to the owner at the owner's address as recorded in the appraisal district records of the appraisal district in which the property is located; or 
(3)	If personal service cannot be obtained: 
a.	By publication at least once; 
b.	By posting the notice on or near the front door of each building on the property to which the violating relates; or 
c.	By posting the notice on a placard attached to a stake driven into the ground on the property to which the violation relates, if the property contains no buildings. 
(b)	If the city mails a notice to a property owner in accordance with subsection (a)(2) above, and the United States Postal Service returns the notice as "refused" or "unclaimed," the validity of the notice shall not be affected, and the notice shall be considered as delivered. 
(c)	In a notice provided under this section, the city may inform the owner by regular mail and a posting on the property that if the owner commits another violation of the same kind or nature that poses a danger to the public health and safety on or before the first anniversary of the date of the notice, the city without further notice may correct the violation at the owner's expense and assess the expense against the property. If a violation covered by a notice under this subsection occurs within the one-year period and the city has not been informed in writing by the owner of an ownership change then the city, without notice, may take any action permitted, and assess the expenses therefore, as provided by section 30-104. 
(Ord. No. 79-125, § 3, 9-19-79; Ord. No. 81-173, § 1(B), 9-2-81; Ord. No. 00-426, § 2, 5-17-00) 
Sec. 30-106. - Collection of expenses. 
    The mayor or city health officer shall file a statement of expenses giving the amount of such expense, the date on which such work was done, and a description of the premises upon which such work was done or improvements made with the county clerk. The city shall have a privileged lien on such lot or real estate upon which such work was done, or improvements made, to secure the expenditures so made, in accordance with Vernon's Ann. Civ. St. art. 4436, as amended, which lien shall be second only to tax liens or liens for street improvements, and such amount shall bear ten percent interest from the date the statement is filed. For any such expense and interest suit may be instituted, and recovery and foreclosure of such lien may be had in the name of the city. The statement of expenses, so made, or a certified copy thereof, shall be prima facie proof of the amount expended for such work or improvements. 
(Ord. No. 79-125, § 4, 9-19-79) 
Secs. 30-107-30-124. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - PRESERVATION OF TREES 

Sec. 30-125. - Definitions. 
    For the purposes of this article, the following words, terms, and phrases shall have the meanings ascribed thereto: 
    Clear cutting shall mean removing more than 50 percent of existing protected trees. 
    Critical root zone of a tree shall mean the area within a circle centered on the trunk location, the diameter of said circle being one-half of the sum of the longest and shortest drip line diameters. 
    Damage shall mean any action that will, in reasonable probability, result in the death of a protected tree, either immediately or within a period of three years. Without limiting this definition, some examples are: severing the main trunk or main limbs or roots, girdling, poisoning, carving, mutilating, touching with live wires; or within the critical root zone: crushing or exposing the roots or digging or drilling any hole or trench larger than three cubic feet, or covering with three inches or more of soil or compacting the soil. 
    Diameter of a tree shall mean the trunk of a tree measured at a point on the tree four and one-half feet above the surrounding ground level. 
    Height shall mean the height of a tree as measured from the trunk at ground level to the highest branches of the tree. 
    Person shall mean any individual, entity, corporation, organization, unincorporated organization, partnership, or any other form of entity. 
    Protected tree shall mean a long-lived, branching, woody plant, usually with one main stem or trunk, and having a diameter of at least eight inches. For the purpose of this article, privets and ligustrums are not considered protected trees. 
    Replacement tree shall mean a long-lived, branching, woody plant, usually with one main stem or trunk, and having a diameter of at least two inches or be 13 feet in height. See section 30-129 for a list of recommended replacement trees. Trees not on the list must be approved by a certified arborist and be indigenous with the area. 
    Structure shall mean that which is built or constructed, an edifice or building of any kind, or any place of work artificially built up or composed of parts joined together in some definite manner. 
    Subject site shall mean any lot, tract, or parcel of land upon which an applicable tree subject to a permit hereunder is located. 
    Tree disposition and replacement plan, or tree survey, shall mean a plan submitted to the building official when land is cleared, elevated, or redeveloped. 
(Ord. No. 09-584, § 3, 12-2-09; Ord. No. 13-635, § 3, 9-11-13) 
Sec. 30-126. - Enforcement. 
    This article shall be administered as a part of the building permit process. There shall be no fee associated with the tree permit. 
(Ord. No. 09-584, § 3, 12-2-09; Ord. No. 13-635, § 3, 9-11-13) 
Sec. 30-127. - Permit required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to remove or to cause damage to a protected tree within the city for new construction, clear cutting, or redevelopment without having first obtained a tree destruction permit from the city. 
(1)	Criteria for issuance of a tree destruction permit. 
a.	An application for a tree destruction permit shall be filed by the owner of the subject site on which an affected tree is located. 
(Ord. No. 09-584, § 3, 12-2-09; Ord. No. 13-635, § 3, 9-11-13) 
Sec. 30-128. - Criteria for tree replacement. 
(a)	A condition for the issuance of each tree destruction permit under this article may include the planting and maintenance of a replacement tree(s) on the subject site or on a site within the community that has been approved by the building official. No tree destruction permit shall be issued incidental to construction, alteration, remodeling, or destruction of any building or structure requiring a building permit, or any subdivision improvement requiring a building permit, unless the applicant therefore has submitted to the building official, designated by the city, and received approval therefor in accordance with this article, a tree disposition and replacement plan, together with a plan for the protection and preservation of each tree impacted by the proposed activity. 
(b)	The scale on the tree disposition and replacement plan shall be no smaller than one inch equaling 20 feet. Trees proposed to be retained are to be represented by a solid circle on the tree survey. Trees proposed to be removed are to be shown by a hatched circle on the tree survey with diameters listed on the plan. Proposed replacement tree(s) shall be shown by a dashed circle with species, diameters and heights listed on the plan. Tree loss protective measures described in section 30-130 shall be taken for all trees subject to danger or loss. 
(Ord. No. 09-584, § 3, 12-2-09; Ord. No. 13-635, § 3, 9-11-13) 
Sec. 30-129. - Replacement trees. 
(a)	Each protected tree considered damaged or permitted for removal requires replacement that is less than 10 inches in diameter may be replaced with a single tree a minimum of two inches in diameter or 13 feet in height. 
(b)	Each protected tree considered damaged or permitted for removal requires replacement that is ten inches or greater in diameter shall be replaced with two trees which are a minimum of two inches in diameter or 13 feet in height. 
(c)	No replacement tree shall be approved by the building official unless it complies with the minimum standards continued herein. 
Recommended Species 
Pecan - Carya illinoensis 
Cedar elm - Ulmus crassifolia 
American elm - Ulmus americana 
Chinese pistache - Pistacia chinensis 
Green ash - Fraxinus pennsylvanica 
Red maple - Acer rubrum 
Winged elm - Ulmus alata 
River birch - Betula nigra 
Southern magnolia - Magnolia grandiflora 
Sweetgum - Liquidambar styraciflua 
Eastern red cedar - Juniperus virginiana 
Bald cypress - Taxodium distichum 
Loblolly pine - Pinus taeda 
American sycamore - Platanus occidentalis 
Bur oak - Quercus macrocarpa 
Cherrybark oak - Quercus falcate var. pagodafolia 
Laurel oak - Quercus laurifolia 
Live oak - Quercus virginiana 
Mexican white oak - Quercus polymorpha 
Nuttal oak - Quercus nuttallii 
Overcup oak - Quercus lyrata 
Post oak - Quercus stellata 
Shumard oak - Quercus shumardii 
Swamp chestnut oak - Quercus michauxii 
Water oak - Quercus nigra 
Willow oak - Quercus phellos 
Sawtooth oak - Quercus acutissima 
Chinkapin oak - Quercus muehelenbergii 
(d)	Time limit for planting replacement trees . Planting of replacement tree(s) shall take place within 12 months. 
(Ord. No. 09-584, § 3, 12-2-09; Ord. No. 13-635, § 3, 9-11-13) 
Sec. 30-130. - Required tree protection. 
    A tree protection plan for trees with a drip line diameter greater than ten feet shall consist of placing an orange net fence around the tree in a manner agreeable to a licensed arborist sufficient to protect the tree roots from damage by activities during construction. 
(Ord. No. 09-584, § 3, 12-2-09; Ord. No. 13-635, § 3, 9-11-13) 
Sec. 30-131. - Appeals. 
    Any person who is aggrieved by a decision of the Taylor Lake Village Tree Advocate or building official hereunder may appeal such decision to the board of adjustments, by filing an appeal with the city secretary, not less than ten days following entry of the decision appealed. Upon such appeal, the building official shall forthwith submit all applicable records and findings to the city secretary as part of the record of such application. The board of adjustments may affirm or deny the decision of the building official. 
(Ord. No. 09-584, § 3, 12-2-09; Ord. No. 13-635, § 3, 9-11-13) 
Sec. 30-132. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Accumulation hazard means any accumulation or collection of water which is not a water feature that results, whether intentionally or unintentionally, in stagnant water that appears to be remain in place for more than ten days. For example, bottles, drums, planters, flower pots, cans, tires, buckets, barrels, bird baths, jars or other receptacles which collect water and are allowed to remain filled with water for long periods of time shall constitute an accumulation hazard. 
    Fountain means a structure which includes apparatus for moving water or which is designed to allow water movement. Fountains with standing water which is green or black shall be presumed to be nonoperational and a public nuisance. 
    Pond means any accumulation or collection of water which acts as a habitat for fish or other aquatic animals, even if this is not its main purpose, with a depth of two feet or less. 
    Stagnant water means any accumulation or collection of water within the city in which mosquitoes breed, or are likely to breed, including but not limited to swimming pools, ponds, water gardens and fountains, unless such collection of water is treated using water treatment methods, as defined in this article. Collections of water which are green or black in color are presumed to be stagnant water and shall be treated as a public nuisance in violation of this article. 
    Swimming pool means any accumulation or collection of water with a depth of more than two feet. 
    Water feature means a pond, water garden, swimming pool, fountain or other intentionally created or maintained collection of water and not located entirely and continuously in an air conditioned space. 
    Water garden means any accumulation or collection of water which is not a pond, whether seasonal or permanent, with a depth of two feet or less, generally used for to grow water plants or for aesthetic purposes. 
(Ord. No. 16-664, § 2, 6-15-16) 
Sec. 30-133. - Criteria for water treatment. 
    Water features must be treated using one of the following methods and must be treated frequently, such that any collection of water within the city is not green, black, or otherwise likely to promote the breeding of mosquitoes: 
(1)	Screening with wire netting of at least 16 meshes to the inch each way, or with any other material which will effectually prevent the ingress or egress of mosquitoes. 
(2)	Complete emptying every seven days of unscreened containers, together with thorough drying and cleaning of the containers. 
(3)	Using a larvicide approved by the United States Environmental Protection Agency. 
(4)	Keeping clean and sufficiently free from vegetative growth and other obstructions, stocking with mosquito eating fish, or providing aeration and circulation of water. 
(5)	Proper disposal, by removal or destruction, of tin cans, tin boxes, broken or empty bottles, containers and similar articles likely to hold water wherein mosquitoes can breed. 
(Ord. No. 16-664, § 2, 6-15-16) 
Sec. 30-134. - Prohibitions. 
    The following shall be prohibited by this article and shall constitute a public nuisance: 
(1)	Accumulation hazards, as defined by section 30-132; 
(2)	Fountains which are not maintained such that water moves continuously at least once each day; 
(3)	Water features which have not been treated or have not been sufficiently treated, as prescribed by section 30-132; 
(4)	Swimming pools which are not compliant with the currently adopted versions of the International Pool and Spa Code and the International Property Maintenance Code, as prescribed in section 10-31; and 
(5)	Ponds or water gardens with a depth of more than two feet. 
(Ord. No. 16-664, § 2, 6-15-16) 
Sec. 30-135. - Enforcement. 
    Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished according to the provisions of section 1-9. If the owner or occupant of any lot or premises shall be a corporation and shall violate any provision of this article, the president, vice-president, secretary or treasurer of such corporation, or any manager, agent or employee of such corporation, shall also be severally liable for any penalty. 
(Ord. No. 16-664, § 2, 6-15-16) 
Sec. 30-136. - Abatement by the city. 
    If any person who owns any lot or building within the city does not abate a nuisance as described in this section within seven days after notice to such person, as provided in section 30-137, the city may do or cause to be done that which will abate the nuisance, and may pay the expense therefore, and charge such expenses incurred in doing such work or having such work done or improvements made to the person who owns such lot or building. If such work is done or improvements made at the expense of the city, such expense shall be assessed on the real property upon which such expense was incurred as provided in section 30-106. 
(Ord. No. 16-664, § 2, 6-15-16) 
Sec. 30-137. - Dissemination of notice. 
(a)	The notice required in section 30-136 shall be given: 
(1)	Personally to the owner in writing; 
(2)	By letter addressed to the owner at the owner's address as recorded in the appraisal district records of the appraisal district in which the property is located; or 
(3)	If personal service cannot be obtained: 
a.	By publication at least once; 
b.	By posting the notice on or near the front door of each building on the property to which the violating relates; or 
c.	By posting the notice on a placard attached to a stake driven into the ground on the property to which the violation relates, if the property contains no buildings. 
(b)	If the city mails a notice to a property owner in accordance with subsection (a)(2) above, and the United States Postal Service returns the notice as "refused" or "unclaimed," the validity of the notice shall not be affected, and the notice shall be considered as delivered. 
(c)	In a notice provided under this section, the city may inform the owner by regular mail and a posting on the property that if the owner commits another violation of the same kind or nature that poses a danger to the public health and safety on or before the first anniversary of the date of the notice, the city without further notice may correct the violation at the owner's expense and assess the expense against the property. If a violation covered by a notice under this subsection occurs within the one-year period and the city has not been informed in writing by the owner of an ownership change then the city, without notice, may take any action permitted, and assess the expenses therefore, as provided by section 30-136. 
(Ord. No. 16-664, § 2, 6-15-16) 
Sec. 30-138. - Collection of expenses. 
    The mayor or city health officer shall file a statement of expenses giving the amount of such expense, the date on which such work was done, and a description of the premises upon which such work was done or improvements made with the county clerk. The city shall have a privileged lien on such lot or real estate upon which such work was done, or improvements made, to secure the expenditures so made, in accordance with V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.007, as amended, which lien shall be second only to tax liens or liens for street improvements, and such amount shall bear ten percent interest from the date the statement is filed. Suit may be instituted for any such expense and interest, and recovery and foreclosure of such lien may be had in the name of the city. The statement of expenses, so made, or a certified copy thereof, shall be prima facie proof of the amount expended for such work or improvements. 
(Ord. No. 16-664, § 2, 6-15-16)
